   able color... as handy as it is handsome and
   satisfying evidence of your good taste. 1

HOW TO GET THE MOST SERVICE
FROM YOUR TELEPHONE
   Whenever you pick up the telephone, you are about to make an impression on
 someone important — the person at the other end of the line., He can’t See'^ypur facial
 expressions or your gestures. He must depend on what you say and how you say it —
 your tone, your inflection, your way of expressing yourself.
    Here, for your consideration, are some suggestions on using the telephone that are
 helping many persons and their companies to make friends.
Before You Call Make Sure
of the Number
A wrong number inconveniences you and
the person called. Consulting this directory
or a personal calling list when not sure of
the number saves time and dispositions.
Apologize For Wrong Numbers
                                               • |
   If a wrong number is (
 reached, an apology helps
 the person called in error \r'~ri
 to feel better about it.
 Hanging up without ac-
 knowledging his Answer
 can be irritating and be-
 wildering to him.
  Place Your Own Calls
  and Be Ready to Talk
  Few business practices
 are more irritating and
 inefficient than that of a
 secretary asking a person
 to hold the line while she
 gets the person who is
 to talk on the line.
Person Called Time to Answer
  The person you call
 may be farther from the
 telephone than you think.
 Allowing enough time to
 answer . . . 10 rings or
 a full minute . . . often
 avoids making another
 call.
 Normal, Natural Tone
 of Voice Is Best
 Shouting distorts your
 voice and isn't pleasant.
  It also is irritating to try
  to understand someone
  who whispers or mum-
  bles or doesn’t talk di-
  rectly into the transmitter.
Leaving Word Keeps
You in Touch
  When you’re to be
away from your phone,
you may avoid losing
important calls and in-
formation if you’ll leave
word where you’ll be and
when you expect to re-
turn.
Hang Up Gently
 Thoughtless slamming
 of the receiver may seem
 an act of discourtesy to
 the person with whom
 you’ve been talking. You
 don’t mean it, of course, but it may leave
 the wrong impression.
Visualize the Other Person
 You're much more apt to be pleasant
 and understanding if you “see” and speak
 TO the person at the other end of the line
 and not TO the telephone.
    Answering Promptly Helps
Complete Call	\
  Immediate atten-__y of :
tion to the tele-	A < m
 phone’s ring pre-
 vents losing the
 call and gets the conversation off on the
 right foot. Answer before the second ring
 if possible.
Identify Yourself When You Answer
and When You Call
     It gets a conversation off to a good start
 when you let the person calling know who
 you are. Say, for example, “Mr. Brown” or
 “Brown speaking”, Roberts Company” or
 “Bates Brothers, C. R. Jones speaicing.”
 It saves time and confusion.
